Russellโs works remain their own best introduction, but there is a large literature on Russell and the various aspects of his 
philosophy, some of which carries much further the debates he started. A. J. Ayerโs [3mBertrand Russell [0m(Fontana, 1972) and [3mRussell 
and Moore; The Analytical Heritage [0m(Harvard University Press, 1971) provide a sympathetic introduction. R. M. Sainsburyโs [3mRussell [0m
(Routledge, 1979) gives an absorbing technical discussion of Russellโs central work. Peter Hyltonโs [3mRussell, Idealism and the 
Emergence of Analytic Philosophy [0m(Clarendon Press, 1990) is essential reading for any serious study of Russellโs thought. Nicholas
